Jamison Brereton

165
Indra and the Maruts
Indra (1, 2, 4, 6, 8, 10тАУ12), the Maruts (3, 5, 7, 9), and Agastya (13тАУ15) 15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
R╠еgveda I.165, 170, and 171 together tell a story in which Indra and the Maruts argue over their rights to a sacrifice offered by the sage Agastya. In the absence of a full, contemporary narrative, it is difficult to reconstruct the events of this story. Apparently AgastyaтАЩs sacrifice was originally intended for the Maruts. Indra arrived at the place of the sacrifice first, however, and complained that nothing was being given to him (170). Agastya, frightened by the god (cf. 171.4), then gave the sacri
fice to Indra. At this point the Maruts arrived expecting that the sacrifice would be offered to them. Agastya tried to appease the Maruts (171), who were understandably angry that the sacrifice had gone to Indra. Indra and the Maruts then confront one another (165), and each side asserts its power and worthiness to receive the sacrifice. Ultimately, however, the Maruts concede IndraтАЩs superiority (165.9), and Indra and the Maruts become reconciled with one another (vs. 11) and share the sacrifice. At the very end of the hymn the poet states one of the reasons that he recalls this story: he hopes to be reconciled to the gods, just as the Maruts were reconciled to Indra. Stanley Insler has proposed the attractive theory that this group of hymns forms a small Aindram─Бruta epic, whose purpose was to justify a ritual change that occurred during the time of the poet. In the classical Vedic ritual the Midday Pressing is dedicated to Indra along with the Maruts, but for much of the core R╠еgveda the Midday Pressing belongs to Indra alone. This narrative tells how the Maruts also came to share the soma along with Indra.
In verse 9d we read kariс╣гy─Б╠Бс╕е with Oldenberg and others, and in verse 15c we read тАЩvay─Б╠Бm, also with Oldenberg.

Jamison Brereton Notes

[I.165 Indra and Maruts (misc. comments by SJ to JPB tr.) This hymn is full of somewhat тАЬoffтАЭ forms, some of them unique to the hymn

– yujmahe (5c), ┼лgr├б- (6c, 10c), cyavam (10d) – a few confined to this hymn and one or a few other passages – vadh─лm (8a), kariс╣гy─Б╠Б(9d). It is not clear to me whether these are the result of faulty transmission or of the poetтАЩs manipulation of form, though I incline towards the latter explanation, given AgastyaтАЩs characteristic selfconscious artfulness. In either case the clustering of these anomalies in a single hymn makes it unlikely in each individual case that they belong to the systematic grammar of Vedic or reflect deep archaisms or old sound changes, as has been suggested for several of them. For further remarks see the individual discussions below.

The trajectory of the hymn might be seen as the battle of the lexicon: words pass back and forth between the two speaking parties, with twists in their usage and with terms that seem to belong to one of the parties appropriated by, or devalued by, the other. Among the most important words are ├йka- тАШalone, onlyтАЩ and the multiple forms of тИЪkс╣Ы тАШdoтАЩ. Note esp. the extraordinary concentration of тИЪkс╣Ы in the middle of the hymn: 7a cakartha, 7c kс╣Ыс╣З├бv─Бm─Б, 8d cakara, 9c kariс╣гy─Б╠Бkс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н, 10b kс╣Ыс╣З├бvai, 11b cakr├б, including two of the rarest pf. forms, 1st sg. cakara and 2nd pl. cakr├б.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra speaks): With what auspicious fortune have the Maruts, who are of one age, one residence, one dignity, watered (the earth) together; with what intention; whence have they come; showerers of rain, they venerate through desire of wealth, the energy (that is genitive rated in the world by rain).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] With what beauty have the MarutsтАФall of the same age, all of the same nestтАФjoined altogether?
With what thought? From where have these antelopes come? With a desire for good things (these) bulls chant explosively.

Jamison Brereton Notes

IтАЩd be inclined to take sam─Бny─Б╠Бnot as an adv. (тАШaltogetherтАЩ) as in the published translation, but as a fem. instr. sg. forming part of the phrase k├бy─Б ┼Ыubh─Б╠Б, hence тАЬwith what joint/common beauty?тАЭ – with the sense тАЬwhatтАЩs their joint insignia? how shall I recognize them?тАЭ Note that sam─Бn├б- is differently formed from the two preceding phonologically similar adjectives s├бvayasaс╕е s├бn─лс╕╖─Бс╕е, which do match each other.

Note also following s├бm m… The adj. sam─Бn├б- returns in 7b in a charged context.

JPBтАЩs tr. cleverly reads ├йt─Бsaс╕е twice, once as the nom. pl. тАШantelopesтАЩ, once as the nom. pl. of the ppl. ─Б╠Б-ita- тАШcome hereтАЩ.

In d ┼Ы├║с╣гс╣Гam may be adverbial as JPB takes it (тАШexplosivelyтАЩ), but it may be a real obj. of ├бrcanti (тАЬchant their explosive powerтАЭ). IтАЩm inclined to follow the latter course, because ┼Ы├║с╣гma- must be a real noun in 4b. But in this case I interpr. it as an Inhaltsakk., further specifying the chant (*тАЬchant their chantтАЭ ├а тАЬchant their explosive forceтАЭ) not the object of their praise as Geldner, for example, does: тАЬpreisen den KampfmutтАЭ (sim. Witzel Got┼Н).

Griffith

WITH what bright beauty are the Maruts jointly invested, peers in age, who dwell together?
From what place have they come? With what intention? Sing they their strength through love of wealth, these Heroes?

Geldner

Mit welchem Aufputz haben sich die altersgleichen, versippten Marut gemeinsam zusammengetan? Mit welcher Absicht, woher sind sie gekommen? Diese Bullen preisen den Kampfmut im Wunsch nach Sch├дtzen.

Grassmann

Mit welchem Schmucke funkeln dort die Maruts in gleicher Pracht, an Alter gleich und Ursprung? Was ist ihr Plan? von wo sind sie gekommen? sie st├╝rmen wild, die Helden, Gut begehrend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOf whose oblations do the youthful (Maruts) approve; who attracts them to his (own) sacrifice (from the rites of others); with what powerful praise may we propitiate (them), wandering like kites in the mid-air?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In whose sacred formulations have the youths found delight? Who turned the Maruts here to the rite,
(thinking,) тАЬBy what great thought shall we bring them to rest, soaring like falcons in the midspace?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Griffith

Whose prayers have they, the Youthful Ones, accepted? Who to his sacrifice hath turned the Maruts?
We will delay them on their journey sweeping–with what high spirit!–through the air like eagles.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The Maruts): Indra, lord of the good, whither do you, who are entitled to honour, proceed alone; what means this (absence of attendance); when followed (by us), you require (what is right); lord of fleet horses say to us, with plural asant words, that which you (have to say) to us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You require what is right: sampс╣Ыcchase = sam─лc─лnam pс╣Ыccase

Jamison Brereton

[Leader of the Maruts:] Why do you travel alone, Indra, although you are great, o lord of the settlements? Is this proper for you?
Confronting us, are you going to negotiate with us beautiful ones? You should tell us what you have for us, o master of the fallow bays.

Griffith

Whence comest thou alone, thou who art mighty, Indra, Lord of the Brave? What is thy purpose?
Thou greetest us when meeting us the Bright Ones. Lord of Bay Steeds, say what thou hast against us.

Geldner

Woher kommst du, Indra, allein, der du doch ein M├дchtiger bist, du rechtm├д├Яiger Herr? Was hast du dabei f├╝r Absicht? Du willst mit uns paktieren, da du mit den Geputzten zusammengetroffen bist. Sag du uns das, o Falbenlenker, was du f├╝r uns hast.

Grassmann

┬╗Warum, o Indra, sonst dich gross erweisend, f├дhrst du allein, o Herr, was liegt im Sinn dir? Wenn du uns pr├дcht’ge triffst, so plauderst gern du? so sprich, was hast du wider uns, o Rossherr?┬л

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ (Indra): Sacred rites are mine; (holy) praises give me plural asure; libations are for me; my vigorous thunderbolt, hurled (against my foes), goes (to its mark); me, do (pious worshippers) proptiate; hymns are addressed tome; these horses bear us to the presence (ofwhose worshippers, and worship).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] The formulations, the thoughts, the pressed soma are good fortune for me. My explosive power rises; the pressing-stone is
brought forth to me.
The hymns hope for, receive me joyfully. These two fallow bays carry us here to them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The act. forms iyarti, etc., are usually transitive, but Oldenberg cites a few passages with the intrans. value that must also be present here.

Although various tr. (e.g., Witzel Got┼Н) take ukth─Б╠Бas acc. pl. and supply subjects for the pl. verbs ─Б╠Б┼Ы─Бsate and pr├бti haryanti (men and gods respectively, Witzel Got┼Н), taking it as nom. pl. not only avoids the need to cast around for unexpressed subjects but also captures IndraтАЩs extreme egotism: even the hymns long for him, or so he thinks.

Griffith

Mine are devotions, hymns; sweet are libations. Strength stirs, and hurled forth is my bolt of thunder.
They call for me, their lauds are longing for me. These my Bay Steeds bear me to these oblations.

Geldner

Mir sagen die feierlichen Reden, die Gedichte, die Somagetr├дnke zu. Der Kampfmut regt sich; der Pre├Яstein ist f├╝r mich aufgesetzt. Die Loblieder w├╝nschen, erwarten mich. Dieses Falbenpaar f├дhrt uns zu ihnen.

Grassmann

┬╗Gebete, Lieder, Tr├дnke, sie erfreun mich, Begier erwacht, der Pressstein ist geschirrt mir; Sie flehn, willkommen sind mir ihre Spr├╝che; und meine F├╝chse fahren uns zum Mahle.┬л

Elizarenkova

рдПрд╡рдореБрдХреНрддрд╛ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рддрдореЗрд╡рдВ рдмреНрд░реБрд╡рддреЗ ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдПрд╡рдВ рдХрд░реЛрд╖рд┐ рдЕрддрдГ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рддреН рд╡рдпрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддрдореЗрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд┐рдХрддрдореИрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ рдпреБрдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢реИрдГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░реЗрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдпрддреНрддрдмрд▓реИрдГред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдорд╣реЛрднрд┐рдГ рддреЗрдЬреЛрднрд┐рдГ рддрдиреНрд╡рдГ рдЖрддреНрдорд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢реБрдореНрднрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рджреАрдкрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдирд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдорд╣реЛрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрди рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рдпрдореН рдПрддрд╛рдиреН рдЧрдиреНрддреВрдиреН рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореН рдЙрдк рдпреБрдЬреНрдорд╣реЗ рддрд╡ рд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рджрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХреБрд░реНрдорд╣реЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдордкрд┐ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛рдореН рдЙрджрдХрдВ рдмрд▓рдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреБ рдмрднреВрде рд╣рд┐ рдЕрд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреЛрджрдХрдЬрдиреНрдпрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреБрднрд╡рд╕рд┐ рдЦрд▓реБ ред рд╣рд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░реЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреЛрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рджреНрдпреЛрддрдирд╛рд░реНрдердГ рее рее реирек рее

English translation:

тАЬ (The Maruts): Therefore we also, decorating our person ns, are ready, with our docile and night-standing steeds, (to attend) you, with all our splendour, to those rites; verily, Indra, you appropriate our (sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You appropriate: svadh─Бm anu hi no babh┼лtha, you have been upon or after our food; or, balam, strength; or, udakam, water; i.e. you seek after the oblations genitive rated either by our strenght, or the water we have created

Jamison Brereton

[Leader of the Maruts:] For this reason, yoking (our chariots) with nearer (horses) that guide themselves and making our bodies
beautiful,
we now yoke antelopes also (as our lead team) by our great powers, for you have experienced our independent will, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

yujmahe is a famous crux: though it should belong to the well-attested root aor. (seen presumably in part. yuj─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е in p─Бda a), it has a primary ending and therefore looks like a pres. formation. It has received a plethora of explanations. Geldner calls it a non-reduplicated perfect (тАЬPerf. ohne Redupl.тАЭ); Whitney (Rts.) simply allows for a root pres. for a few forms, incl. this one, in addition to the standard root aor. Probably the currently prevailing interpr. is HoffmannтАЩs (MSS 2 [1952/1957]: 130-31 =Aufs. II: 366), that it shows dissimilatory loss of the first nasal from

*yu├▒jmahe belonging to the nasal-infix pres. Although this explanation has a plausible foundation (as opposed to GeldnerтАЩs motiveless non-redupl. pf.), the coexistence of yujmahe with yuj─Бn├б- in the same verse, and the general trickiness of AgastyaтАЩs poetry, incline me to a nonce, contextual explanation. The oddly placed n├║ тАШnowтАЩ (though see 9a) immediately following the verb form and ending the p─Бda seems AgastyaтАЩs signal that heтАЩs twisted and tweaked the aorist to his own ends – a temporary present. Thanks to Jesse Lundquist for assembling the relevant lit. and for illuminating disc.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra seizes the MarutsтАЩ assertion of independent power (svadh─Б╠Б- 5d) by taxing them with the absence of (their exercise of) that power (6a) at a crucial moment. Another skirmish in the battle of the lexicon.

Griffith

Therefore together with our strong companions, having adorned our bodies, now we harness,
Our spotted deer with might, for thou, O Indra, hast learnt and understood our Godlike nature.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra): Where, Maruts, has that (sacrificial) food been assigned to you, which, for the destruction of Ahi was appropriated to me alone; for I indeed am fierce and strong, and mighty, and have bowed down all mine enemies with death-dealing shafts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] Where was this independent will of yours, Maruts, when you tasked me alone to smash the serpent?
For I, the powerful and mighty, possessed of might, humbled with my weapons those of every rival.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the length in ┼лgr├б- here and 10c. Lubotsky (2000 [тАЬVedic root vс╣Ы тАж,тАЭ Indoarisch, Iranisch und die Indogermanistik]: 320 n. 16) attributes it to compensatory lengthening from *h├н uHgr├бs, after laryngeal metathesis from *hi Hugr├бs, but I find the proposed metathesis counterintuitive (despite the other exx. he adduces); one would rather expect the laryngeal to remain where it is as a hiatus-filler. Moreover, assuming that this remained as a synchronic rule in the RV is quite hard to accept.

Indra adroitly manipulates the wording here to contrast his own solitary state with the MarutsтАЩ collectivity: тАж m─Б╠Бm ├йkaс╣Г sam├бdhatta тАЬтАж me alone together youтАжтАЭ

05-06 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra seizes the MarutsтАЩ assertion of independent power (svadh─Б╠Б- 5d) by taxing them with the absence of (their exercise of) that power (6a) at a crucial moment. Another skirmish in the battle of the lexicon.

Griffith

Where was that nature then of yours, O Maruts, that ye charged me alone to slay the Dragon?
For I in truth am fierce and strong and mighty. I bent away from every foeman’s weapons.

Geldner

Wo war denn diese eure Selbst├дndigkeit, ihr Marut, als ihr mich im Drachenkampf allein lie├Яet? Denn ich, der Gewaltige, Starke, ├Ьberlegene parierte jedes Feindes Waffen mit meinen Waffen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The Maruts): Showerer (of benefits), you have done much; but it has been without united equal energies; for we, too, most powerful Indra, have done many things, and by our deeds (we are, as) we desire to be, Maruts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Leader of the Maruts:] You did many things when we were there, with our united manly powers (ready) to be deployed, o bull;
we shall do many things in accordance with your purpose, o most
powerful Indra, when we, o fellow Maruts, shall wish it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In vs. 5 the Maruts spoke literally of yoking their teams to bring them for the journey, but in this vs. the same root тИЪyuj is used metaphorically, in the gerundive y├║jya-, to indicate the MarutsтАЩ powers that were available to be yoked/deployed by Indra, though he didnтАЩt. Note also the adj. sam─Бn├б- тАШcommon, jointтАЩ (repeated from 1b) referring to the powers shared by the Maruts, in contrast to IndraтАЩs constant lone state.

The question in this vs. is whose kr├бtu- do the Maruts plan to follow. Acdg. to the JPB tr., it is IndraтАЩs, but the tr. canтАЩt stand exactly as given for syntactic reasons.

Because marutaс╕е is unaccented, either kr├бtv─Б has to belong to the y├бd clause or marutaс╕е has to belong to the main cl. But the published translation assigns marutaс╕е to the dependent cl. and kr├бtv─Б to the main cl: тАЬwe shall do many things in accordance with your purpose, o most powerful Indra, when we, o fellow Maruts, shall wish it.тАЭ Following the two syntactically licensed alternatives above, we must rather tr. either тАЬWe shall do many things, o most powerful Indra, when, o Maruts, we shall wish it in accordance with our/your will.тАЭ Or тАЬWe shall do many things, o most powerful Indra, in accordance with your/our will, o Maruts, when we shall wish it.тАЭ kr├бtv─Б is perfectly placed for maximum ambiguity, between Indra and the Maruts. Taking it with the main cl. (the 2nd alternative tr. just given) favors an interpr. of IndraтАЩs will; taking it with the subord. cl. (the 1st alternative) favors the MarutsтАЩ will. That, I think, is the correct interpr. The Maruts contrast IndraтАЩs actions, which were performed with the MarutsтАЩ standing by on the scene, with their own prospective actions, which will depend on their own intention, not IndraтАЩs design or timetable.

The dueling vocatives in d, ├нndra and marutaс╕е, are notable, esp. because they encase the word kr├бtv─Б whose crucial ambiguity we have just discussed. Since we must assume that the 1st

-ps. speaker is a Marut or Maruts, the pl. vocative to the group is of course striking – though well within the limits of poetic self-address we find elsewhere in the text (see disc. in my “Poetic Self-Reference in the Rig Veda and the Persona of Zarathustra,тАЭ Fs. Skjaerv├╕, 2009). In this case I imagine a тАЬspokesMarutтАЭ who takes the lead in addressing Indra but also turns to his own group for a chorus of affirmation (of the type, тАЬright, guys?!тАЭ).

Griffith

Yea, much hast thou achieved with us for comrades, with manly valour like thine own, thou Hero.
Much may we too achieve, O mightiest Indra, with our great power, we Maruts, when we will it.

Vieles hast du mit uns als Verb├╝ndeten, mit vereinten Kr├дften, du Bulle, getan. Vieles werden wir drum noch tun, du gewaltigster Indra, wenn wir ernstlich wollen, ihr Marut.

┬╗Gar viel hast du vollbracht mit uns verb├╝ndet o starker, mit vereinten Heldenkr├дften, Und vieles werden wir, o Indra, wirken mit Kraft, o st├дrkster, wenn wir Maruts wollen.┬л

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra): By my own prowess, Maruts, I, mighty in my wrath, slew Vс╣Ыtra; armed with my thunderbolt, I created all these pellucid genitive ly-flowing waters for (the good of) man.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] O Maruts, I smashed Vr╠еtra with my Indrian strength, having become mighty through my own rage.
Bearing my mace in my arms, I made these all-gleaming waters go easily to Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Injunctive 1st sg. v├бdh─лm belongs to the root aor. stem of this seс╣н root, whose well-attested 2nd and 3rd sg. are (├б)vadh─лs, (├б)vadh─лt. The 1st sg. should be *vadham, which is nowhere attested. The -─л- has simply been imported from the 2nd/3rd sg.; v├бdh─лm is attested once elsewhere in the RV, in the late hymn X.28.7.

The juxtaposition of maruta indriy├йс╣Зa recalls the immediately preceding (7d) ├нndra тАж marutaс╕е.

P─Бda-final vi┼Ыv├б┼Ыcandr─Бс╕е produces an irregular cadence of four heavy syllables; three of the remaining four occurrences of the stem occur in the same position (though once in dimeter vs.) and have the same effect. As is often remarked, the cmpd. would be metrically regular if the 2nd member were the related -candra, hence *vi┼Ыv├бcandr─Бс╕е with the light 2nd syllable appropriate to a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence.

The same problem afflicts the other cmpds of -┼Ыcandra- (├б┼Ыva-, sv├б-, h├бri- and puru-, su-), which either show up in metrically indifferent positions or positions in which a light 2nd syllable would be favored (besides Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence, also right after an opening of 4, where a break ╠Ж- - is distinctly bad). There are no forms where the meter is improved by reading -┼Ыcandra-. Although the obvious solution is simply to read *-candra-, I am puzzled as to how the -┼Ыcandra- forms won out. The duplicate pair ┼Ыcandr├б- / candr├б- are for the most part in complementary distribution, with candr├б- an independent adj. and 1st cmpd member and ┼Ыcandr├б- 2nd cmpd member (after vowel); ┼Ыcandr├б- appears 3x uncompounded, but in these cases it is in a sequence that functions like a quasi-cmpd (pur├║ ┼Ыcandr├бm III.31.15, pс╣Ыth├║ ┼Ыcandr├бm IV.2.13, and possibly ├бdhi ┼Ыcandr├бm VIII.65.11). So vi┼Ыv├б-┼Ыcandra- has the expected alternant, though in almost all cases a metrically unfavorable one. Must we reckon with a replacement of the originally correct -┼Ыcandra- by *-candra-, yielding a metrically usable form, and then redactional restoration of the -┼Ыcandra-? This hypothesis seems over-complex, but I donтАЩt have a better one. In any case the poet seems to be toying with the form: the next p─Бda (8d) contains the offending sequence ┼Ыc, though split across a word boundary (ap├б┼Ы cakara), and in 12c a candr├б- compd., candr├б-varс╣З─Б(с╕е) occupies the same p─Бda-final slot. Its initial also participates in the ┼Ыc sequence: maruta┼Ы candr├б-, so that the first member is effectively *┼Ыcandr├б-.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The Maruts): Verily, Maghvan, nothing (done) by you is unavailing; there is no divinity as wise as you; no one being born, or that has been born, ever surpasses the glorious deeds which you, mighty (Indra), have achieved.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Verily, Maghavan: anuttam─Б te maghavan nakir nu na = whatever is said by you, Indra, is true;

Anuttam─Б = an exclamation or assent that which is not sent or driven away

Jamison Brereton

[Leader of the Maruts:] This is conceded to you, generous one: There is no one like you known among the gods.
Neither one who is born nor one who was born will attain you. What *you will do, do!тАФo you who are grown fully strong.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The form kariс╣гy─Б╠Бis problematic for several reasons. Despite its sandhi position before k, it seems best to assume it represents 2nd sg. kariс╣гy─Б╠Бs out of sandhi, even though kariс╣гy─Б╠Бс╕е would be the proper sandhi form in this context. (The Pp.

simply reads kariс╣гy─Б╠Бlike the Saс╣Гhit─Б text, but the standard tr. and comm [e.g., Oldenberg, going back to BR] take it as 2nd sg.) Moreover, this form must be a subjunctive to the future stem, an unusual morphological combination at best (but see Whitney, Grassmann

┬з938). Reading the transmitted kariс╣гy─Б╠БwonтАЩt help: that would simply be a 1st sg. subj.

to the future, or perhaps a 2nd sg. imperative to the future, neither of which is any better morphologically. The other long-shot possibility is to assume itтАЩs an unusual gerundive formation in -iс╣гy├б- in the neut. nom.-acc. pl., yielding тАЬwhat things are to be done тАжтАЭ (so S─Бyaс╣Зa.). AiG II.2.368 mentions this possibility but prefers the subjunctive interpr.

Griffith

Nothing, O Maghavan, stands firm before thee; among the Gods not one is found
thine equal.
None born or springing into life comes nigh thee. Do what thou hast to do, exceeding mighty?

Geldner

An die dir zugestandene Macht, o Gabenschenker, reicht keiner je heran - nicht ist einer, der dir gliche, unter den G├╢ttern bekannt - weder einer, der noch geboren wird, noch ein Geborener. Was du vorhast, das tu, du Erstarkter!

Grassmann

┬╗Nichts ist f├╝rwahr, o Held, dir unbezwinglich, dir gleich gibt’s keinen unter allen G├╢ttern, Kein lebender, kein fr├╝herer erreicht dich, so thu, o starker, was zu thun du vorhast.┬л

рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЖрд╣ред рдореЗ рдордо рдПрдХрд╕реНрдп рдЪрд┐рддреН рдПрдХрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рднреБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░рдЧрдордирд╢реАрд▓рдореН рдУрдЬрдГ рдмрд▓рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдмрд▓рдореН рдПрдХрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддреБ рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердорд┐рддрд┐ рдЪреЗрддреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрд╛ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдордиреАрд╖рд╛ рдордиреАрд╖рдпрд╛ рдордирд╕рдГ рдИрд╖рдпрд╛ рджрдзреГрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдзрд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╣рдВ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдХреГрдгрд╡реИ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдЕрд╣рдВ рд╣рд┐ рдЕрд╣рдВ рдЦрд▓реБ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрдмрд▓рдГ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдирдГ рд╡реЗрджрдирд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐ рдЪреНрдпрд╡рдВ рдЕрд╡рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдорд┐ рдПрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЕрд╣рдореЗрд╡ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЗрддреН рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдПрд╡ рд╕рдиреН рдИрд╢реЗ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЛ рднрд╡рд╛рдорд┐ ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдиреЛрд╜рд╣рдВ рдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЪреНрдпрд╡рдВ рдпрд╛рдиреНрдпреБрджреНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдп рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдпрдВ рдПрд╖рд╛рдореАрд╢реЗ ред рдпрддреЛрд╜рд╣рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрддрдГ рд╢рдХреНрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рее реирел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra): May the prowes of me alone be irresistible; may I quickly accomplish whatever I contemplate in my mind; for verily, Maruts, I am fierce and sagacious and to whatever (objects) I direct (my thoughts), of them I am the lord, and rule (over them).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] Even if I am alone, let my force be far ranging (to do) what in my daring I shall now do according to my inspired thinking,
for I am known as the powerful one, Maruts. What things I shall set in motion, just I, Indra, am master of these.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In most tr. the rel. cl. of p─Бda b seems loosely construed with the main clause of p─Бda a, with the y─Б╠Бreferring to an unexpressed acc. of respect in the main cl.: тАЬLet my force be far-reaching with regard to (those things), which I will do тАжтАЭ However, the vertical parallelism of 9d, 10b, and 10d suggests a different syntactic arrangement 9d y─Б╠Бni [kari]с╣гy─Б╠Бkс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н тАж 10b y─Б╠Бn├║ [dadhс╣Ы]с╣гv─Б╠Бn kс╣Ыс╣З├бvai тАж 10d y─Б╠Бni Not only do these p─Бdas match phonologically as in the display above, but 9d and 10d show the same syntactic structure: a preposed rel. cl. introduced by an acc. pl.

referring to deeds and a verb governing it referring to the doing of the deeds (y─Б╠Бni

*kariс╣гy─Бс╕е; y─Б╠Бni cyavam), followed by a main clause where the doer of the rel. clause is also subject: kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н, ─л┼Ы─У. I suggest 10b should be interpr. in the same general pattern. Indra says тАЬWhich (deeds) (I am) bold (to do), I will do.тАЭ In other words, p─Бda b contains two clauses, not one, and is independent of the preceding p─Бda.

The 1st sg. cyavam is the only non-causative active form to this root.

Hoffmann (Injunk. 247-48) takes it as a subjunctive, an ersatz for the unenlarged 1st sg. subj. ending -─Б. I agree that the form has been tampered with, but would suggest that what really underlies the form may be medial subjunctive 1st sg. *cyavai, which should have yielded *cyav─Б in this sandhi position. The -m serves as a pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ hiatus filler (perhaps originally -m╠Р). An alternative that would work better phonologically is to assume a 1st sg. indicative *cyave, not a subjunctive. This would yield *cyava in sandhi, to which the -m could be added without adjusting the vowel length. Since the verb in the main cl., ─л┼Ыe, is likewise present indicative (as opposed to impv. kс╣Ыс╣Зuh├н in 9d and subjunctive kс╣Ыс╣З├бvai in 10b), an indicative in the subord. cl.

would match.

Griffith

Mine only be transcendent power, whatever I, daring in my spirit, may accomplish.
For I am known as terrible, O Maruts I, Indra, am the Lord of what I ruined.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, on this occasion praise delights me; that prise which is to be heard (by all), which men have offered me. To Indra, the showerer (of benefits), the object of pious sacrifice; to me, (endowed) with many forms (do you) my friends (offer sacrifices) for (the nourishment of my) person n.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The praise song here has exhilarated me, o Maruts, the formulation worthy to be heard that you created for me, o menтАФ
for me, (who am) Indra, the bull and strong combatantтАФfor (me), your companion as my companions, for me myself by you yourselves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The final p─Бda of this vs. brings the vocabulary into reciprocal alignment and thus signals that harmony has been restored: s├бkhye s├бkh─Бyas tanv├и tan┼л╠Бbhiс╕е.

Griffith

Now, O ye Maruts, hath your praise rejoiced me, the glorious hymn which ye have made me, Heroes!
For me, for Indra, champion strong in battle, for me, yourselves, as lovers for a lover.

Geldner

Begeistert hat mich dabei euer Lob, ihr Marut, die Erbauung, die ihr Herren mir bereitet habt, wert zu h├╢ren, mir dem Indra, dem Bullen, dem Freigebigen, dem Freund die Freunde in eigener Person meiner Person.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, verily, glorifying me, and enjoying boundless fame and food (through my favour), edo you, of golden colour, and invested with glory, cover me in requital verily, (with renown).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It is just so: Reflecting me here and receiving fame and refreshments as my irreproachable (warrior band),
you, who are to be seen all around with your shimmering colors, have pleased me, and you will please me now, o Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The med. part. d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е is generally tr. тАШreceivingтАЩ, as the middle voice of тИЪdh─Б often is, and interpr. to mean that the Maruts also get fame as part of IndraтАЩs reflected glory (see pr├бti тАж rocam─Бn─Б(с╕е) in a). But in this charged context of tributes given and received, I think it likely that it is ambiguous. Indra is both graciously yielding the Maruts some glory, but he is also reminding them that they have just produced praise for him (vs. 11) and will presumably continue to do so. In this second sense it could be tr. тАЬsetting out praise (for me)тАЭ with the middle voice reflecting the mutually intertwined relationship between Indra and the Maruts.

With most interpr. I take ├бnedyaс╕е as a nom. sg. m. implicitly modifying an unexpressed gaс╣З├бс╕е тАШtroopтАЩ, a construcio ad sensum with the pl. d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е. I would like to find some way to ally it with n├йd─лyas- тАШnearerтАЩ, as a neut. sg. modifying ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е, but this seems beyond the realm of possibility.

The saс╣Гc├бkс╣гy─Б of the Saс╣Гhit─Б text is read saс╣Гcakс╣гya by the Pp. and taken as a gerund, an interpr. followed by Oldenberg inter alia. The meaning would be тАЬhaving looked upon (me)тАЭ vel sim. Grassmann (fld. by Geldner [Witzel Got┼Н], etc., incl. the published translation) takes it as a gerundive, whose pausal form would be saс╣Гc├бkс╣гy─Бс╕е. Both forms are possible. I do not have a strong feeling either way.

On -┼Ы candr├б- see disc. ad 8c.

Note the p─Бda-final n┼лn├бm, reminiscent of n├║ in 5c and 9a.

Griffith

Here, truly, they send forth their sheen to meet me, wearing their blameless glory and their vigour.
When I have seen you, Maruts, in gay splendour, ye have delighted me, so now delight me.

Geldner

Diese, die mir also entgegenstrahlen, die untadelige Schar, die sich Ruhm und Speisegen├╝sse zulegen - ihr Marut, goldfarbig aussehend habt mit jetzt gefallen und sollt mir auch zuk├╝nftig gefallen.

Grassmann

So wie ihr seid hier, mir entgegenstrahlend, mit hohem Ruhm und Kraft begabt, untadlig, Wenn ich euch seh’, o Maruts, hellergl├дnzend, gefielt ihr mir, gefallet ihr mir jetzt auch.┬л

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдХреЛ рдиреБ рдЦрд▓реБ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрдГ рдордорд╣реЗ рдкреВрдЬрдпрддрд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕рдЦрд┐рд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рдЦреАрдиреН рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рд╕рдЦрд┐рднреВрддрд╛рдиреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреБрдВ рдкреНрд░ рдпрд╛рддрди рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдд ред рд╣реЗ рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЪрд╛рдпрдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдордиреНрдорд╛рдирд┐ рдордирдиреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдкрд┐рд╡рд╛рддрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рднреВрдд рднрд╡рдд ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдореЗ рдорджреАрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдПрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЛрддрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрд╡рд┐рддрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдирд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ рднреВрдд рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╛рд░реЛ рднрд╡рдд рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Agastya): What mortal, Maruts, worships you in this world; hasten, friends, to the presence of your friends; wonderful (divinities), be to them the means of acquiring riches, and be not uncognizant of my merits.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Be not uncognizant: eс╣г─Бm bh┼лta naved─Б me с╣Ыt─Бn─Бm = be cognizant of these my truths, mad─лy─Бn─Бm avitath─Бn─Бm j├▒─Бt─Бro bhavata

Jamison Brereton

[Narrator:] Now who has given liberally to you here, Maruts? Journey forth to your companions here, o companions!
Knowing our thoughts intimately, o you shimmering ones, be aware of these, my truths.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The reciprocal lexical harmony of s├бkh─лn тАж sakh─Бyaс╕е recalls that found in 11d s├бkhye s├бkh─Бyaс╕е, but there is a small mystery: the voc. pl. sakh─Бyaс╕е surely refers to the Maruts, but who are the plural expressed by s├бkh─лn? We would expect a singular referring to Indra. It seems unlikely to be the priests plus/minus Indra because the speaker is a singular (note me in d, the sg. inter. prn. k├бс╕е in the rhetorical question in p─Бda a, and the sg. poet in vs. 14). I take that speaker to be Agastya (contra the published translation, which identifies him as the narrator). Perhaps a pl. maiestatis for Indra? If n├бved─Б(с╕е) belongs to the s-stem n├бvedas-, it should be nom. m. singular here, in disagreement with the plural subj. of bh┼лta. GrassmannтАЩs solution is to set up a them.

stem n├бveda- for just this passage, which would allow a plural interpr. To avoid this ad hoc multiplication of stems, we can assume the same type of constructio ad sensum invoked for ├бnedyaс╕е in the immed. preceding vs. (12b)(so Oldenberg), with the sg.

referring collectively to the Marut troop. Cf. also the parallel passage IV.23.4 dev├│ bhuvan n├бved─Б ma с╣Ыt─Б╠Бn─Бm, with a legitimate singular; the post-caesura portions of the p─Бdas are identical. On the origin of n├бvedas- from a false segmentation of -tana v├йdas- see Schindler, Fs. Knobloch, 1985.

Griffith

Who here hath magnified you, O ye Maruts? speed forward, O ye lovers, to your lovers.
Ye Radiant Ones, assisting their devotions, of these my holy rites he ye regardful.

Geldner

Wer feiert euch wohl hier, o Marut? Fahret zu den Freunden, ihr Freunde! Wecket die Gedanken, ihr Pr├дchtigen: Nehmet diese meine rechten Worte wahr!

Grassmann

Wer ist’s, der euch, o Maruts, jetzt verherrlicht? o kommt doch her, ihr Freunde, zu den Freunden, O gl├дnzende, belebend unsre Andacht und werdet Zeugen meiner frommen Werke.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince the experienced intellect of a venerable (sage), competent to bestow praise upon (you), who deserve praise, has been exerted for us; do you, Maruts, come to the presence of the devout (worshipper), who, glorifying (you), worships you with these holy rites.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Indra:] Since the praise poet will here offer friendship (to you) as if to his friend, (and since) the wisdom of the son of M─Бna [=Agastya]
has brought us here,
turn here to the inspired poet, o Maruts. The singer chants these
formulations for you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich of this vs. is quite problematic; see OldenbergтАЩs long disc. The problems lie in the verbs (or apparent verbs). The pf. cakr├й in b only makes sense in this context if it is construed with the preverb ─Б╠Бin p─Бda a: ─Б╠БтИЪkс╣Ы тАШmake (to come) here, bring hereтАЩ. By contrast, the verbal stem duvasy├б- is never otherwise construed with ─Б╠Б, even though it appears to be here. Moreover, the recipient of the friendship offered by the verb duvasy├б- is always in the accusative, not the apparent dat. duv├бse here. (Note also that the suffix-accented duv├бs- appears only here and in nearby I.168.3. It seems to show the regular possessive sense of s-stem adjectives built to sstem neuters by accent shift: hence d├║vas- тАШfriendshipтАЩ ├а duv├бs- тАШpossessing friendship, friendтАЩ.) The best solution seems to me RothтАЩs suggested emendation of duvasy─Б╠Бd to *duvasy─Б╠Б, instr. of an abstract in -y─Б╠Б, an emendation endorsed by Oldenberg

Hence I would alter the published translation to тАЬWhen/Since the wisdom of the son of M─Бna has brought us here with friendship, like a bard to a friendтАЭ vel sim. The emendation only requires de-gemination of the -d d- and has no effect on the meter; the addition of a -d might have been encouraged by the repetitive phonological pattern in a (which I will represent with false word division): y├бdduvas y─Б╠Б(d)duv├бs(e). Note also the dental geminate in vartta in c, where the double -tt- may have been restored etymologically (since Rtt and Rt generally fall together). Although there is no nominal stem *duvasy─Б╠Б-, there is the variant duvoy─Б╠Б-, showing external sandhi (see AiG I.343), also appearing as in instr. (V.36.6, perhaps not coincidentally in an Indra hymn in a vs. addressed to the Maruts).

Griffith

To this hath Manya’s wisdom brought us, so as to aid, as aids the poet him who worships.
Bring hither quick! On to the sage, ye Maruts! These prayers for you the singer hath recited.

Geldner

Da wie die Zuneigung zu einem G├╝nstling der Dichter, die Sehergabe des Manya uns hergef├╝hrt hat, so kehret, o Marut, fein bei dem Redekundigen ein! Diese erbaulichen Worte soll der Dichter f├╝r euch anstimmen.

Grassmann

Wenn wie zur Spende euch der Dichter herlockt, und der Gesang des weisen uns herbeizog, So wendet bald euch, Maruts, her zum Beter, f├╝r euch ja sang der S├дnger diese Spr├╝che.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis praise, Maruts, is for you; this hymn is for you, (the work) of a venerable author, capable of conferring delight (by his laudations). May the praise reach you, for (the good of your) person ns, so that we may (thence) obtain food, strength, and long life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Capable of conferring: m─Бnd─Бyasya k─Бroс╕е: the epithet is stutivi┼Ыeс╣гair mandayituс╕е; or, stutibhir madasya prerayituс╕е, causer of plural asure by praises; food, strength and long life: iс╣гam vс╣Ыjanam j─лrad─Бnum: j─лrad─Бnum = jaya┼Ы─лlam d─Бnam, donation connected with victory; the hymn is repeated at the end of the next s┼лkta; where it is explained as: cirak─Бla j─лvanam, long life

Jamison Brereton

[Narrator:] This is your praise song, MarutsтАФthis song of the praise poet M─Бnd─Бrya, son of M─Бna.
With his refreshing offering he would beg *reconciliation (with you) for himself. тАУ May we know refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the tr. assumes underlying avay─Б╠Бm (тАШvay─Б╠Бm in sandhi) тАШpropitiationтАЩ. This does not require emendation to the Saс╣Гhit─Б text, since the word appears after vowel-final tanv├й.]

Griffith

May this your praise, may this your song, O Maruts, sung by the poet, Mana’s son, Mandarya,
Bring offspring for ourselves with food to feed us. May we find strengthening food in full abundance!

Geldner

Dies Preislied, diese Lobrede des Dichters Mandarya, des Maniden, ist f├╝r euch, Marut. Er m├╢chte durch Nahrungsf├╝lle f├╝r seine Person zu Nachwuchs gelangen. - Wir m├╢chten einen gastfreien Opferb├╝ndler kennen lernen, der rasch schenkt.

Grassmann

Euch, Maruts, gilt dies Lied des Manasohnes, das Lob des Dichters von dem Stamm Mand─Бra’s, Mit Labung kommt herbei zu eigner St├дrkung gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрдд рдПрд╖ рд╡рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореЛ рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдХрд╛рд░реЛрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдЧреАрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рд╕реБ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╕реНрддрдиреНрд╡ рдЗрд╖рд╛рд╜рд╜рдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╖реНрдЯ рд╡рдпрд╛рдорд┐рд╖рдВ рд╡реГрдЬрдирдВ рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрд╖рдГ) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рд╕реНрддреЛрдордГ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд╕рдореВрд╣рдГ (рдорд░реБрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрддрдорд╛рдГ (рдЗрдпрдореН) рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ (рдЧреАрдГ) рд╡рд╛рдЧреН (рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдорд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдпреЛрддреНрддрдордЧреБрдгрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЪ (рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдкреВрдЬрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрд╕реНрдп (рдХрд╛рд░реЛрдГ) рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдирдГ (рдЖ) (рдЗрд╖рд╛) рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрдпрд╛ (рдпрд╛рд╕реАрд╖реНрдЯ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╛рддреНрдордиреЗрдкрджрдореНред (рддрдиреНрд╡реЗ) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рд╛рдп (рд╡рдпрд╛рдореН) рд╡рдпрдореНред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкреАрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рд▓рднреЗрдорд╣рд┐ (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) рдмрд▓рдореН (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН рее резрел рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдп рдЖрдкреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд▓рдмреНрдзреНрд╡рд╛ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдорд╛рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЬрдиреНрдорд╕рд╛рдлрд▓реНрдпрдорд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее резрел реердЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрдмреЛрдзреНрдпрд╛ реердЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╖рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рдбреНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ реердЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рд╡рд╕реБрд░реБрджреНрд░рд╛рджреНрдпрд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереИрд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдЖрдкреНрдд, рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮ, рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛, рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереА рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрдЧрддреАрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░реВрди рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рдЪреЗ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд, рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рдЬрдиреНрдо рд╕рдлрд▓ рдЕрд╕рддреЛ, рд╣реЗ рдЬрд╛рдгрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резрел рее
